<script>
  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_fd294b3b-101d-49fa-a33f-b9250cf39db2'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };
    if (typeof AppleID !== "undefined") {
      initAppleId();
    } else {
      initializeSiwa();
    }

  <span id="freeText18214361172528054708" style="display:none">Matilde Martínez es una pediatra decidida a cambiar el mundo. Eliah Al-Saud es un soldado profesional, demasiado cínico para creer que es posible cambiarlo. Sin embargo, cuando Eliah y Matilde se conocen, la atracción es innegable, y, pese a sus diferencias, caen rendidos ante la pasión que los domina. Su romance se convertirá en una aventura peligrosa, con el conflicto palestino-israelí y una amenaza atómica como telones de fondo. Una adictiva novela contemporánea en la que dos personajes intensos y cautivadores lucharán por sus vidas y las de sus seres queridos, pero ¿conseguirán también salvar su amor?</span>

<div id="review_592080839" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/592080839" />
    <a title="Beth" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5375148-beth"><img alt="Beth" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1583841703p2/5375148.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/592080839?book_show_action=true">Apr 16, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Beth" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Beth" href="/user/show/5375148-beth">Beth</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781612184357" href="/book/show/17140862-obsession">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5375148-beth?shelf=netgalley">netgalley</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5375148-beth?shelf=own">own</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5375148-beth?shelf=urban">urban</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5375148-beth?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5375148-beth?shelf=mystery">mystery</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5375148-beth?shelf=thriller">thriller</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer592080839" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2542534668045580057">A very rich, powerful, mercenary and Saudi prince meets humanitarian, pediatric surgeon on a plane to Paris and they become completely Obsessed with each other..<br/><br/>After meeting Matilde Martinez, Eliah Al-Saud ruthlessly pursues the romantically naïve surgeon. Matilde is overwhelmed and discourages Eliah's attentions but still fantasizes about him a way she has never desired a man before. With an unhealthy attraction, their romance explodes. <br/><br/>Little did Eliah and Matilde know that their lives have a</span>
  <span id="freeText2542534668045580057" style="display:none">A very rich, powerful, mercenary and Saudi prince meets humanitarian, pediatric surgeon on a plane to Paris and they become completely Obsessed with each other..<br><br>After meeting Matilde Martinez, Eliah Al-Saud ruthlessly pursues the romantically naïve surgeon. Matilde is overwhelmed and discourages Eliah's attentions but still fantasizes about him a way she has never desired a man before. With an unhealthy attraction, their romance explodes. <br><br>Little did Eliah and Matilde know that their lives have already have been intertwine by lies, deceit, and very deadly political games. <br><br>I'm going to tell you right off the bat, I'm very conflicted about this book. So, I'll start with my issues... <br><br>Eliah. Every time I thought I'd find something redeeming about him, he ended up digging himself deeper into highly dislike character category. I finally found an alpha that pushed me over the edge of too much.<br><br>Matilde. Matilde is going to the Congo, one of the worst, unstable countries in the world but she can't handle some of the circumstances that arise in Paris. I also wasn't crazy with Matilde's acceptance of Eliah mental mistreatment and his desire for force a negative reaction from her. I can not see Matilde supposed inner strength that was reiterated to us throughout the story.<br><br>What I adored...<br><br>The story was extremely complex with a vast amount of interwoven characters and plots that masterfully come together into a brilliantly designed story line.<br><br>Florencia Bonelli highly descriptive writing, making you feel like you are right there in the center of each and every scene as it takes place.<br><br>I really didn't like the main characters but was thrilled by the story that surrounded them. I was utterly intrigued by the combination of history, current political situations and the fictitious twist created Bonelli. White knuckled suspense with a shocking open ending, <i>Obssesion</i> couldn't help but capture the mystery thriller lover in me.<br><br>This ARC copy of <i>Obsession</i> was given to me by Amazon Publishing - AmazonCrossing in exchange for a honest review. This book is set for publication on July 23, 2013.<br><br>Written by: Florencia Bonelli<br>Series: Year of Fire<br>Sequence in Series: 1<br>Paperback: 612 pages<br>Publisher: AmazonCrossing <br>Publication Date: July 23, 2013<br>ISBN-10: 1612184359<br>ISBN-13: 978-1612184357<br>Age Recommendation: Adult<br>Genre: Mystery Thriller Romance<br>Rating: 3.75 Stars<br><br>Find this book on:<br><a href="http://www.amazon.com/Obsession-Year-Fire-Florencia-Bonelli/dp/1612184359/ref=tmm_pap_title_0?ie=UTF8&amp;qid=1371168592&amp;sr=8-1" rel="nofollow noopener">Amazon</a><br><a href="http://www.barnesandnoble.com/w/obsession-florencia-bonelli/1114559179?ean=9781612184357" rel="nofollow noopener">Barnes &amp; Noble</a><br><br><i>For more reviews check out <a href="http://www.tometender.blogspot.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Tome Tender's Book Blog</a> or find us on <a href="http://facebook.com/TomeTender" rel="nofollow noopener">Facebook</a>.</i><br><div>

<div id="review_674269005" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/674269005" />
    <a title="starsaga" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7499703-starsaga"><img alt="starsaga" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1366832600p2/7499703.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/674269005?book_show_action=true">Jul 22, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="starsaga" class="user" itemprop="url" name="starsaga" href="/user/show/7499703-starsaga">starsaga</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781612184357" href="/book/show/17140862-obsession">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7499703-starsaga?shelf=a-a-owned">a-a-owned</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7499703-starsaga?shelf=favorite-author">favorite-author</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7499703-starsaga?shelf=5-star-romance-reads">5-star-romance-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7499703-starsaga?shelf=a-a-reviewed">a-a-reviewed</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer674269005" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer690036500455580757"><b>5 stars for this story, it was a captivating read!</b><br/>What a great journey through the lives of Eliah and Matilde! It started with tension and ended with the same and in between the story of these two surprisingly likeable people captured me. Although quite cliched and vaguely disconnected on some occasions, the structuring of this book was very good. This was for two reasons, one, was simply Eliah. Somehow, the Hero is a super-spy-merc-hot-guy who is quite the family man, this I liked because the a</span>
  <span id="freeText690036500455580757" style="display:none"><b>5 stars for this story, it was a captivating read!</b><br />What a great journey through the lives of Eliah and Matilde! It started with tension and ended with the same and in between the story of these two surprisingly likeable people captured me. Although quite cliched and vaguely disconnected on some occasions, the structuring of this book was very good. This was for two reasons, one, was simply Eliah. Somehow, the Hero is a super-spy-merc-hot-guy who is quite the family man, this I liked because the author very skillfully made Eliah not so much of an isolated fighting machine as spy heroes often are, and in doing so humanized him for me, made him more real. The second reason this story was good for me, was because although the ending was not the best possible, it was still satisfying and for a 600+ page book, I thought it ended in a place that allows the characters a little room to grow. They need that, in my opinion.<br />The action suspense part of the book made little impact on me, there was a lot going on, but I would not read this book for espionage thriller suspense with chases and gunfights. This is not that story. The best part of this book for me was not in getting history lessons either, it was in the high-strung powerful relationship that these two very different people were trying to have. There was a lot of dialogue in this book and it was sometimes bumpy because it was clear this is a translation, in trying to stay true to the moment or the expressions of the original, sometimes the nuances of English that would have been helpful, were missing. Nevertheless, this book charmed me for its novelty in the setting, the characters, perhaps not so much the passionate romance, but definitely for intriguing me enough to want to read the continuation. I recommend this book and am anticipating the next one.</span>
  <a data-text-id="690036500455580757" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer822310269" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7942149525766691551">It's rare to find a Trilogy or even a Novel that has all the elements I want in a romance novel but this one has it all, historical content, realistic story lines and characters, passionate and deep, deep love, adventure, strong male figures, skilled and strong heroes, rescues, angelic compassionate women, excitement, heartbreak, friendship and just an all out good story. <br/><br/>It's all there in this Trilogy, Book One, (Obession) Year of Fire by Florencia Bonelli. She's from Argentina and is an extrem</span>
  <span id="freeText7942149525766691551" style="display:none">It's rare to find a Trilogy or even a Novel that has all the elements I want in a romance novel but this one has it all, historical content, realistic story lines and characters, passionate and deep, deep love, adventure, strong male figures, skilled and strong heroes, rescues, angelic compassionate women, excitement, heartbreak, friendship and just an all out good story. <br /><br />It's all there in this Trilogy, Book One, (Obession) Year of Fire by Florencia Bonelli. She's from Argentina and is an extremely talented author. There's a small hill to get over after the initial meeting of the main characters before it gets going, mostly because of the technical and scientific details and a lot of political themes going on but it's a part of what makes the story realistic and believable. <br /><br />Few couples are portrayed as having the type of relationship I appreciate and crave to read but Florencia has pulled it off with Matilde and Eliah Al-Saud. What a pleasure it is to have found another novel of the same caliber. </span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">

<span id="freeTextContainer5496913208119322581">Whew, what a long read. I love long books- lots of room for plot, character building, etc. I have to give this 4.5*. There are so many characters, that it slowed the flow for me. I agree with Starsaga, I love the H, Eliah, what a hunky solid anti-hero-hero- flaws and all. I got used to the translation, as I got into the book. I love novels based on history, other country, cultures. I read another novel a few years ago that took place in Spain, and originally written in Spanish- so I got used to </span>
  <span id="freeText5496913208119322581" style="display:none">Whew, what a long read. I love long books- lots of room for plot, character building, etc. I have to give this 4.5*. There are so many characters, that it slowed the flow for me. I agree with Starsaga, I love the H, Eliah, what a hunky solid anti-hero-hero- flaws and all. I got used to the translation, as I got into the book. I love novels based on history, other country, cultures. I read another novel a few years ago that took place in Spain, and originally written in Spanish- so I got used to the different expressions translated to English. I appreciated the research that Florencia did for the technical parts of the plot. I know it is difficult to translate accurately from Spanish to English- but I just hope book 2 (Congo) comes out soon.</span>

<div id="review_678679558" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/678679558" />
    <a title="Roxanne Smith" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/17008803-roxanne-smith"><img alt="Roxanne Smith" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1373126116p2/17008803.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/678679558?book_show_action=true">Jul 27, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Roxanne Smith" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Roxanne Smith" href="/user/show/17008803-roxanne-smith">Roxanne Smith</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781612184357" href="/book/show/17140862-obsession">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/17008803-roxanne-smith?shelf=5-stars">5-stars</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer678679558" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8777768472632797029">Read more of my reviews at <a target='_blank' rel='noopener nofollow' href='http://roxannereadsromance.blogspot.com'>http://roxannereadsromance.blogspot.com</a>.<br/><br/>I absolutely loved this very long and suspenseful book! It is a whopping 611 pages so it has plenty of time to develop all the characters. The main female character is Matilde, a pediatric surgeon, who is from Buenos Aires, Argentina. She is in the airport, about to go to Paris to learn French, with her best friend and fellow doctor, Juana. They are taking an intensive French language class to prepare for a trip to the Congo, whe</span>
  <span id="freeText8777768472632797029" style="display:none">Read more of my reviews at <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://roxannereadsromance.blogspot.com">http://roxannereadsromance.blogspot.com</a>.<br /><br />I absolutely loved this very long and suspenseful book! It is a whopping 611 pages so it has plenty of time to develop all the characters. The main female character is Matilde, a pediatric surgeon, who is from Buenos Aires, Argentina. She is in the airport, about to go to Paris to learn French, with her best friend and fellow doctor, Juana. They are taking an intensive French language class to prepare for a trip to the Congo, where they plan to work as medical missionaries. On the flight, Matilde meets Eliah Al-Saud, who is a Saudi Arabian prince with an Italian mother, who principally lives in France. He is a great character, with many facets to his life, his past and his character. Of course, he is a very strong, very protective male who takes over the young doctor's life in a short time. He was a military pilot and now is involved in many secretive military activities. Matilde is very beautiful, smart but vulnerable and they fall in love fast, despite their many differences. It turns out that their families have known each other for many years, which brings complications. One of the many things I like about this book is that even though it has the typical storyline of a not so wealthy younger woman with an older, wealthy man, they both have been married before meeting. Also, the author does a wonderful job describing the many locales in which the story takes place, including Paris, London, Amsterdam, Tel Aviv and more. The story has a lot of dramatic twists and turns and plenty of steamy scenes. The book also has a host of secondary characters to make the story interesting, including Juana, Matilde's BFF, Eliah's friend, Shiloah, who is an Israeli politician, Roy, Maltilde's husband and good friend of her father, Celine, Matilde's sister and a top European model. Both Eliah and Matilde keep secrets from each other, that come out near the end of the story, leading to some dramatic consequences which set up the next part of the trilogy, which takes place in the Congo. The Spanish version of Obsession (Year of Fire) book came out about two years ago and the second part of the trilogy is also out in Spanish. I looked all over for news of the Congo book being translated, but can't find it. I hope it is translated soon. The third part is called Gaza, and I can't find it in Spanish or English, yet. I really look forward to reading the rest of this great love story.<br /><br />Ms. Bonelli is from Argentina and writes her books in Spanish, so this book was translated with mostly good results. Some of the translation is a bit off, such as Eliah refers to his mom as his "old lady." To native English speakers, old lady commonly refers to a girlfriend, not a mother. But, all in all, the translation is well done. And, for the $3.99 on Amazon, you can have many hours of reading fun! Obsession (Year of Fire) can be bought on Amazon and from other booksellers. It is called Caballo de Fuego in the Spanish version, which means "Horse of Fire," which refers to the type of Chinese zodiac sign Eliah was born under and his secret name he uses at work.<br /><br /><br /><br />FIVE STARS</span>
  <a data-text-id="8777768472632797029" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <a title="Writer" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/18428631-writer"><img alt="Writer" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1388794464p2/18428631.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/690605493?book_show_action=true">Aug 09, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Writer" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Writer" href="/user/show/18428631-writer">Writer</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781612184357" href="/book/show/17140862-obsession">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer690605493" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11406724842250604012">I WISHED I READ THE FIRST REVIEWS BEFORE I BOUGHT THIS! 2.5 Star, August 2, 2013<br/><br/>Amazon Verified Purchase<br/>This review is from: Obsession (Year of Fire) (Paperback)<br/><br/>I wish I had read first reviews first before I got this book or I would have known it's a trilogy. It is 611 pages, nothing about the synopsis had said it would come in 3 parts. To wait until next year for the rest is a complete turn off, I don't mind if they come in trilogy or even pentalogy as long as it's clearly indicated.<br/><br/>If you are </span>
  <span id="freeText11406724842250604012" style="display:none">I WISHED I READ THE FIRST REVIEWS BEFORE I BOUGHT THIS! 2.5 Star, August 2, 2013<br /><br />Amazon Verified Purchase<br />This review is from: Obsession (Year of Fire) (Paperback)<br /><br />I wish I had read first reviews first before I got this book or I would have known it's a trilogy. It is 611 pages, nothing about the synopsis had said it would come in 3 parts. To wait until next year for the rest is a complete turn off, I don't mind if they come in trilogy or even pentalogy as long as it's clearly indicated.<br /><br />If you are truly into Gulf War, Mercenary Soldiers, Sarin nerve gas poisoning and the devastating effect of it; notorious evil powers such as Saddam Hussein and weapons of mass destruction, then this is for you. Keeping up with so many names of characters which isn't easy ( foreign middle eastern names ) to keep up with the events, you may need to start writing them down or you'll be lost in the shuffle. There were too many unnecessary events that could have been contracted and would have made the story perhaps easier to follow. Out of 611 pages, about 50% only was dedicated to the love affair of Eliah and Matilde, true it has some actions and tense moments with limitless foreign names to remember, but if you were looking for an easy read with inspiring events and relatable characters, you may want to consider looking into another.<br /><br />The love affair between Eliah Al-Saud and Matilde was what held my interest, even then, I was not impressed with Matilde's character, she has too many baggage, she's weak in her resolve and comes out feigned and spurious despite the repeated glowing description of her being ethereal in beauty and blah blah...she just comes out too needy.<br /><br />Eliah on the other hand is one exceptional man, a former mercenary soldier, once an elite French soldier who did everything exceptionally over the top, has great rigid discipline and self control but somehow loses it where Matilde is concerned. The love relationship between them is almost too good to be true and hard to believe especially Matilde being less than honest, keeping the devastating truth from Eliah, facts she's well aware of that are significantly important to him. Matilde's insincere, deceiving and pretentious self drove me nuts at times but Eliah's overwhelming love and desire for her, his inner turmoil and uncertainties, listening to his POV about his desperate and tormented soul and the constant fear deep in the pit of his stomach feeling Matilde is unattainable, just pierced my heart...this beautiful extraordinary man deserve an equally beautiful, honest, strong spirited woman with loving heart ...definitely not Matilde.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="11406724842250604012" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer4227866936393188987"><b>To be honest, this book was a bit boring.</b><br/> <br/>The main characters meet on a flight to Paris and its automatic sparks for them…. <i>Well, more so on Eliah’s part since he mercilessly ppursues Matilde until she finally agrees to go out with him...Hah..</i> <br/><br/><b>So their backgrounds:</b> Eliah Al-Saud, is a business mogul who comes from a rich and powerful family. <i>And oh, he just so happens to be of royal lineage too.</i><br/><br/>Matilde, on the other hand, comes from a humble background and is a young doctor dreaming of helping t</span>
  <span id="freeText4227866936393188987" style="display:none"><b>To be honest, this book was a bit boring.</b><br /> <br />The main characters meet on a flight to Paris and its automatic sparks for them…. <i>Well, more so on Eliah’s part since he mercilessly ppursues Matilde until she finally agrees to go out with him...Hah..</i> <br /><br /><b>So their backgrounds:</b> Eliah Al-Saud, is a business mogul who comes from a rich and powerful family. <i>And oh, he just so happens to be of royal lineage too.</i><br /><br />Matilde, on the other hand, comes from a humble background and is a young doctor dreaming of helping those in need in Africa.<br /><br /><b>So the story in a jiffy:</b> Eliah and Matilde embark on a tumultuous courtship where power, secrets, and deadly enemies come into play and threaten to tear them apart and their lives. <i>Sounds generic eh?</i><br /><br /><b>My thoughts:</b><br />Basically throughout the story there was A LOT going on at once. Most of the story there was a lot of politics and power talk that made me often skim over.<br /><br />Eliah's character seemed like a lot of rich moguls I read about: arrogant, aggressive, and possessive. He's also quite obsessed with Matilde which is ridiculous at times since I don't seem to feel what connection grounds them together other than their serious attraction for one another. <br /><br />And Matilde. Matilde is an angel. There is no bad qualities about her that I could pick up on other than she's quite frail due to health issues. Matilde is beautiful [even though she often gets downplayed as being much younger than she really is], petite, but also has a heart of gold.<br /><br />I literally felt through their relationship that Eliah was the Big Bad Wolf hunting poor little miss Red Riding Hood since literally that's how Eliah's demeanor was towards Matilde. He smothered Matilde which really bothered me at times since he was really territorial and overbearing of her. <br /><br /><b>Spoiler and rant alert continued:</b><br /><b>AND LASTLY,</b> how can you even consider dating and sleeping with a girl when you were previously sleeping with her sister as your on again-off again sleeping buddy in the past!! Gross!! Then again, Matilde didn't know it at the time since Eliah and Celine's [Matilde's sis] "relationship" was kept hush hush.</span>

<div id="review_621022256" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/621022256" />
    <a title="Tanya Santiago" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5723012-tanya-santiago"><img alt="Tanya Santiago" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1338328014p2/5723012.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/621022256?book_show_action=true">May 21, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Tanya Santiago" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Tanya Santiago" href="/user/show/5723012-tanya-santiago">Tanya Santiago</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781612184357" href="/book/show/17140862-obsession">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5723012-tanya-santiago?shelf=arcs-reviewed">arcs-reviewed</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer621022256" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8138100331183655440">Although this book started off very slow in the beginning, it picked up about half way through. I must honestly say that I was intrigued by the plot and how the characters were interwoven into the story. There was romance, conspiracies, and terrorism which made the story interesting and not to mention it was based in Paris and the author was great at describing the scenery.<br/><br/>The story centers around Matilde and Eliah who meet on a flight to Paris. Matilde is a pediatrician who is ultimately going </span>
  <span id="freeText8138100331183655440" style="display:none">Although this book started off very slow in the beginning, it picked up about half way through. I must honestly say that I was intrigued by the plot and how the characters were interwoven into the story. There was romance, conspiracies, and terrorism which made the story interesting and not to mention it was based in Paris and the author was great at describing the scenery.<br /><br />The story centers around Matilde and Eliah who meet on a flight to Paris. Matilde is a pediatrician who is ultimately going to the Congo to treat sick children. Eliah is the owner of a security company who kind of reminds me of an Arabic Jason Bourne. Despite their differences, they end up falling in love. At this point the story takes so many twists and turns that I had to re-read chapters just to make sure that I didn’t miss anything. And although the main characters were Matilde and Eliah, the story followed other characters in the book and kept switching back and forth. Like I said, I had to re-read to make sure I didn’t miss anything. <br /><br />I won’t give too much away, but the ending is a cliff hanger. It was good a story, but a little too long. I will read the next book when it comes out in English because I am anxious to see what happens between Matilde and Eliah. <br /><br />I’ll give this book 3 out of 5 stars. Like I said, I liked the plot and the characters but the story in my opinion dragged on a little too much.<br /><br />A copy of this book was provided by NetGalley in exchange for an honest review.<br /></span>

          </span>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/664145157?book_show_action=true">Jul 10, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Shad" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Shad" href="/user/show/5982630-shad">Shad</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781612184357" href="/book/show/17140862-obsession">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer664145157" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4140464349268521214">I really want to give this book 4 stars or maybe 3.5, but damn why are there so many characters!!!<br/><br/>I'm reading the book now and to be honest I've lost all momentum to finish it. This is due to the fact that I'm working so hard to remember who all these new characters are that keep coming into the story, geesh! I'm counting 15 people that have been introduced into the story so far and about 4-5 have some immediate connection to our two lovers. I never thought I would ever type this or say this abo</span>
  <span id="freeText4140464349268521214" style="display:none">I really want to give this book 4 stars or maybe 3.5, but damn why are there so many characters!!!<br /><br />I'm reading the book now and to be honest I've lost all momentum to finish it. This is due to the fact that I'm working so hard to remember who all these new characters are that keep coming into the story, geesh! I'm counting 15 people that have been introduced into the story so far and about 4-5 have some immediate connection to our two lovers. I never thought I would ever type this or say this about a book before but there are waaayy too many details in this story. Too much unnecessary background info about people that are introduced for like a millisecond and them poof! there gone until 5 chapters later when they are brought up again. By then I've already forgotten all about them. It takes away from the love affair. It has gotten to the point where I just skip whole passages until I come across one of the main characters names.<br /><br />I want to finish this book, but damn it's starting to feel like homework which is a shame because when I started I was so hooked from the very first paragraph. The writing is great, but I feel like I'm reading two stories at the same time. One international thriller/suspense and the other is a romance novel. It's just not meshing together well enough for me. </span>

Someone mentioned that the hero in this book is possessive, so I was excited to received this one.<br /><br /><i>dum dum dum dum</i><br /><br />I just want to say that I'm so disappointed with the book.. The story is just boring and the dialogue was a bit off that I was struggling to finish it! I noticed this was originally in spanish version and I'm wondering if the author just used a google translator for this.<br /><br />I like all the characters, Matilde is great, she's nice and sweet! Eliah is possessive, short tempered and flawed. I love the possessive and powerful feeling he has for Matilde but other than that the story was flat! <br /><br />The only exciting part in this book was Eliah and Celia, they've been lovers for years and the little confrontation that revealed everything. I was actually expecting more from it, like maybe a cat fight or shoot Eliah.. or Matilde... anyone!... just give me something here coz I'm bored! But nope.. the heroine just sulked and Eliah spent most of his time trying to woo her back.<br /><br />I guess with all the politics and power is just not my cup of tea.<br /><br />Oh.. and the book ends with a cliffhanger.. how nice.</span>
  <a data-text-id="16371093745910921742" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7534408-artemiz?shelf=netgalley">netgalley</a>,

<span id="freeTextContainer10063102083456772724">It's more like 3.5, since it was a bit better than just good book but I can't say that I really liked it. I had no idea what I was getting myself into when I requested this book from NetGalley :).<br/><br/>Well, first of all, it's translated from Spanish to English, thats why sometimes there are some odd archaic/clinical words, or maybe it was just in the ARC I was reading. But it just gave some other level to this story with all the French and Italian and Arabic and German. And it's over 600 pages and it</span>
  <span id="freeText10063102083456772724" style="display:none">It's more like 3.5, since it was a bit better than just good book but I can't say that I really liked it. I had no idea what I was getting myself into when I requested this book from NetGalley :).<br /><br />Well, first of all, it's translated from Spanish to English, thats why sometimes there are some odd archaic/clinical words, or maybe it was just in the ARC I was reading. But it just gave some other level to this story with all the French and Italian and Arabic and German. And it's over 600 pages and it's just first book of the trilogy.<br /><br />But the main impression that I got from this story - imagine that <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/3892.Tom_Clancy" title="Tom Clancy" rel="nofollow noopener">Tom Clancy</a> has written a NA romance, that instead of some extremely dangerous bomb for Jack Ryan to defuse there is an extremely explosive hazardous relationship and when it goes gaboom at the end, as was expected, there is still hope for them in next book. <br /><br />Or imagine that Clancy is invited to write Argentinian telenovella, so beside over the top romance, secrets, emotions, reactions, relationships, jealousy, obsession, there is also war, poisons, politics, killing, kidnapping, secret ops and just like with those telenovellas it all feels too much and after every episode you promise not to continue watching but once you start watching/reading you can't stop, you want to know how it ends. <br /><br />In a way it's classical romance/erotica story where head of the security company falls in love with a timid doctor who wants to heal the world, they both have secrets and they both had fallen in love the first time and they both have been hurt badly before, but before the end they hit the rock bottom with all their secrets coming out and now only time will tell (and next two books) will they be together or not. He is the ultimate male - tall, dark, piercing eyes, fit, extremely protective - and she is the angel come to earth and every man that comes to contact with her (unless they are gay or deeply in love with somebody else) fall for her and want to possess her, and she notices nothing besides her man. <br /><br />It was interesting and enchanting read and I do want to know how it ends, so I have to find time to read the next books.</span>
  <a data-text-id="10063102083456772724" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer837882740" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3825684653705664251">The Year of Fire is an enlightening and brilliant read. It is because of series such as Year of Fire that I fell in love with Romance novels. The character development, the depth of story, and the writing are all so magnificently executed that I found my self lost in the love story between Elia and Matilde and neglecting my own love story. <br/><br/>This novel is not flowery or cheesy. Florencia Bonelli, an Argentine novelist, takes you on a journey from Paris, to the Congo, to the middle east following t</span>
  <span id="freeText3825684653705664251" style="display:none">The Year of Fire is an enlightening and brilliant read. It is because of series such as Year of Fire that I fell in love with Romance novels. The character development, the depth of story, and the writing are all so magnificently executed that I found my self lost in the love story between Elia and Matilde and neglecting my own love story. <br /><br />This novel is not flowery or cheesy. Florencia Bonelli, an Argentine novelist, takes you on a journey from Paris, to the Congo, to the middle east following the passionate and sometimes desperate love of Elia and Matilde. <br /><br />In Year of Fire, Bonelli not only entertains, but she informs about such things as Colton: an essential mineral used in cell phones that is mined in the Congo, which is one of the primary reasons why the people of the Congo have been subject to genocide. And vaginal flagellation: a severe crime against women caused by violent rape, where in which, the anal and vaginal cavities tear, creating one massive opening between the vagina and the anus.<br /><br /> My heart was obviously pained reading this, because in my happy little life in America, atrocities such as this are not apart of my reality. Nevertheless, I am grateful to Florencia for enlightening me on such things, because information is power. <br /><br />I believe the best Romance novels should entertain and inform. Otherwise it is just smut. </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer6494409834679115505">Romance written by an Argentinian author. I didn't get very far into it, although the book is so long that I actually read what would have been half a normal book. <br/><br/>It was a sort of cross between a sheikh romance (the hero is half Saudi, half Argentinian) and a medical romance (the heroine is a pediatrician about to go off to Congo with a Médecins Sans Frontières-type outfit), with a heroine who, pediatrician or not, is horrendously Anastasia Steele-like in her childlike-ness and naiveté. Add to </span>
  <span id="freeText6494409834679115505" style="display:none">Romance written by an Argentinian author. I didn't get very far into it, although the book is so long that I actually read what would have been half a normal book. <br /><br />It was a sort of cross between a sheikh romance (the hero is half Saudi, half Argentinian) and a medical romance (the heroine is a pediatrician about to go off to Congo with a Médecins Sans Frontières-type outfit), with a heroine who, pediatrician or not, is horrendously Anastasia Steele-like in her childlike-ness and naiveté. Add to that a huge dollop of the Israeli-Palestinian conflict, and this is like no romance novel I've ever read. <br /><br />The romance was vomit-inducing, but all the rest (and there is a lot) was strangely interesting. Not interesting enough for me to continue, though. I actually meant to keep reading, but since it's been about 6 weeks since I've managed to force myself to pick it up, I'd best call it a DNF.</span>

  <span id="freeText7690858801413247483" style="display:none">Very entertaining! I found a lot of similarities to the 50 Shades of Grey book minus the playroom. Something that got my attention and could not figure out the reason: why the Spanish used in large parts of the books is Mexican? The author is from Argentina... there were no Mexican characters in the books (I read the trilogy). If the reason is because the rest of Latin America would not understand Argentine slang, then why not use Spanish from the Real Academia Espanola??? It changed the expressions for me. I can't imagine two girls from Argentina wearing chongos and chanclas!!!! (which I had to go to the dictionary to find out that is Mexican for rodetes y sandalias or hair bun and sandals) <br />Otherwise, you can't put these books down. They consume you, nothing else matters!!</span>

  <span id="freeText13688123467033497485" style="display:none">A friend of mine read all three of these books in Spanish, with very different titles, and she highly recommended them to me. I'm reading the 2nd book now, which seems a bit better so far, just because I spent so much money on these books.   function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('zIoQufhf+gv1yv4+E3KakbIHoCjiZF0iSvkpAeEMsPKjYQ7dJI5TJx13UfX0+tsveSgO7Imk0HPy2pZF2hEuAQ==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('AJAGYgezOJJF73UF/toUbrqaBGJchmndYIdyIObbCYFvexgG22KRvq1S2s4ZUlXQcbWqpjdG5IzYpM1k3caXcg==')})
  }

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer18271362403790464848">Florencia Bonelli nació el 5 de mayo de 1971 en la ciudad de Córdoba, Argentina. Estudió Ciencias Económicas y se recibió de contadora pública, profesión que abandonó después de leer El Árabe de Edith Hull, libro que la impulsó a dedicarse profesionalmente a la escritura.<br/><br/>La publicación de su novela épica en dos volúmenes, Indias Blancas (2005), significó un salto en su carrera, logrando atravesar </span>
  <span id="freeText18271362403790464848" style="display:none">Florencia Bonelli nació el 5 de mayo de 1971 en la ciudad de Córdoba, Argentina. Estudió Ciencias Económicas y se recibió de contadora pública, profesión que abandonó después de leer El Árabe de Edith Hull, libro que la impulsó a dedicarse profesionalmente a la escritura.<br /><br />La publicación de su novela épica en dos volúmenes, Indias Blancas (2005), significó un salto en su carrera, logrando atravesar las fronteras de su país, con una potente historia sobre indios y criollos. Sus novelas históricas logran conquistar los rankings de ventas en la Argentina y en el exterior. Su obra ha sido publicada en España, Alemania, Portugal y en toda América Latina.<br /><br /><br />ENGLISH:<br /><br />Florencia Bonelli was born on May the 5th, 1971 in Córdoba city, Argentina.<br /><br />She studied to become an Accountant, and she finally abandoned her Accountant profession when a book that changed her life (The sheik by Edith Hull) showed her that she wanted to become a writer.<br /><br />The publication of White Indian Women (2005), her epic novel in two volumes, marks a before and after in her writing career, expanding her fame beyond her country’s frontiers. Her historical novels have conquered bestseller lists in Argentina and all over the world. Her work has been published in Spain, Germany, Portugal and all of Latin America.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="18271362403790464848" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>
